                        </mrow>
                     </mrow>
                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex"> &lt;math altimg="urn:x-wiley:26379368:media:cey2503:cey2503-math-0024" wiley:location="equation/cey2503-math-0024.png" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"&gt;&lt;mrow&gt;&lt;mrow&gt;&lt;mo&gt;\unicode{x02206}&lt;/mo&gt;&lt;msub&gt;&lt;mi&gt;E&lt;/mi&gt;&lt;mi mathvariant="normal"&gt;b&lt;/mi&gt;&lt;/msub&gt;&lt;/mrow&gt;&lt;/mrow&gt;&lt;/math&gt;</annotation>
                  </semantics></math> of pure defect carbon is 1.003 eV, while the energy barrier of sodium-ion diffusion insertion and extraction of F-doped defective carbon structure decreases to 0.824 eV, indicating a modification of ionic conductivity. F has the strongest electronegativity, which can weaken the exclusion of sodium-ion insertion and extraction to improve its diffusion kinetics, leading to a significant reduction of the charge transfer resistance of the electrode, as evidenced by the following in situ EIS tests.</div>
            
            <p>In theory, F-doping can lead to the transformation of the sp<sup>2</sup>–carbon bond to the sp<sup>3</sup>-state, which is conducive to structural stability. However, excess F also has a negative effect on the electrochemical performance. With defect carbon as the main body, doping models (CF1, CF2, and CF3, respectively) with 1, 2, and 3 F atoms were constructed, and the Na atom was set up to measure the length changes of F–C and C–C bonds after adsorption, so as to investigate the deformation degree of the structure, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a> and Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>. The length of the C–C bond remained almost constant across all structures, varying by only 0.01 Å. The average bond length of F–C in CF3 increases from the original 1.360 to 1.516 Å during the sodiation process, while that of CF1 only increases by 0.011 Å, which explains the unsatisfactory cycling stability of the FHCT<sub>3</sub> electrode.<span><sup><a href="#cey2503-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2503-bib-0044_R_d76722569e1591" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - Adv Energy Mater">44</a></sup></span></p>
            
            <p>In conclusion, F-doping can effectively strengthen the adsorption capacity of sodium ions and reduce the diffusion energy barrier for their migration, but excessive F-doping will cause severe deformation of the anode material during sodiation/desodiation, leading to a drastic reduction of structural stability.<span><sup><a href="#cey2503-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2503-bib-0020_R_d76722569e1596" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Prog Energy Combust Sci">20</a></sup></span></p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="cey2503-sec-0070">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="cey2503-sec-0070-title">2.5 Interphase characteristic regulation</h3>
            
            <p>Recent doping-optimization strategies for hard carbon have mainly focused on the exploration of the intrinsic physicochemical properties of the material, but little attention has been paid to the electronic structure modulation of hard carbon, which can affect its ability to reduce electrolytes, consequently influencing the composition, homogeneity, morphology, and mechanical properties of the SEI films.</p>
            
            <p>Interestingly, it is found that the F-doping of hard carbon not only optimizes the microstructure but also plays a modulating role in the decomposition of electrolytes. To clarify the correlation between the F-doped electrodes and the SEI film properties, the elemental state and composition differences in SEI films formed on the PHC and FHCT<sub>2</sub> electrodes with 50-cycled in ether-based electrolyte were investigated by depth-profiling XPS. From Figures&nbsp;<a href="#cey2503-fig-0006">6A–C</a> and&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, it can be seen that the C element in the SEI film on the FHCT<sub>2</sub> electrode drops remarkably with increasing etching depth (~34% at etching 2 s and ~23% at etching 20 s), while Na and F elements show the opposite trend, directly indicating the formation of an organic-dominated exterior and NaF-rich interior SEI film, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a>. Meanwhile, the atomic ratio of F in the FHCT<sub>2</sub>-based SEI film is significantly higher than that of PHC; it can be speculated that F on the F-doped electrode may be involved in the formation of SEI film. To verify this conjecture, we also detected the F content on the surface of a 50 well-cyclyed FHCT<sub>2</sub> electrode in an F-free electrolyte by the XPS technique (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a>).</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="cey2503-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/4e4a4bb8-9f3f-428d-ac76-134a319a2caf/cey2503-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/4e4a4bb8-9f3f-428d-ac76-134a319a2caf/cey2503-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/004aead3-d866-47c1-a70d-f3cb3cf6e106/cey2503-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/4e4a4bb8-9f3f-428d-ac76-134a319a2caf/cey2503-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=cey2503-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fcey2.503" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Depth-profiling XPS measurements for cycled electrodes. The calculated proportion of SEI film components: (A) the corresponding atomic ratios of C, O, F, and Na in the FHCT<sub>2</sub> electrode system. The corresponding ratio of (B) NaF and (C) Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>. High-resolution XPS spectra of the SEI film formed on (D, E) PHC and (F, G) FHCT<sub>2</sub> electrodes after Ar etching for different etching times.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            
            <p>As shown by the fitting results in Figures&nbsp;<a href="#cey2503-fig-0006">6D–G</a> and&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a>, the main peaks identified in the C 1s, O 1s, F 1s, and Na 1s spectra are roughly similar on cycled electrodes, attesting that the species of SEI film components formed on the hard carbon electrode is mainly dependent on the electrolyte.<span><sup><a href="#cey2503-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2503-bib-0045_R_d76722569e1669" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Adv Funct Mater">45</a>-<a href="#cey2503-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2503-bib-0047_R_d76722569e1669" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Adv Mater">47</a></sup></span> The C 1s peak at 284.55 (C–C, C═C), 285.40 (–CH<sub>2</sub>–), and 286.60 eV (C–O), and the O 1s peak at 532.20 (C═O) and 533.40 eV (C–O) are assigned to organic RCH<sub>2</sub>ONa, which are generated from the reduction of solvents. The C 1s peak at 289.80 eV (CO<sub>3</sub>), the O 1s peaks at 531.30 eV (Na-O), and the F 1s peak at 684.68 eV (Na–F) corresponded to the inorganic components Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, Na<sub>2</sub>O, and NaF, respectively. Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, Na<sub>2</sub>O, and Na–O–F (O 1s at 536.20 eV) are the reduction products of the NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>-solvent complex, and NaF is mainly generated from the decomposition of NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>. In addition, a large amount of C–F (C 1s at 288.50 eV, F 1s at 688.70 eV) that&nbsp;existed in SEI film represents fluorinated organic species, and especially, the FHCT<sub>2</sub> electrode-derived SEI film could be derived from diglyme–SO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>– complex. It has been reported that fluorinated organics can improve the electrochemical stability of hard carbon anode by preventing the dissolution or continuous reactions of SEI film components, consistent with the cycling performance of electrodes. It is noteworthy that the proportion of inorganic species in the SEI film on the FHCT<sub>2</sub> anode is significantly higher than that in the SEI film on the PHC anode due to the modulation of the SEI film by the electronic structure change caused by F-doping.<span><sup><a href="#cey2503-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2503-bib-0043_R_d76722569e1709" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Energy Environ Sci">43</a></sup></span> Especially for NaF, the content of FHCT<sub>2</sub> is nearly double that of PHC. Inorganic species in SEI film generally have low activation energies for sodium-ion diffusion.<span><sup><a href="#cey2503-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2503-bib-0048_R_d76722569e1714" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Adv Mater">48</a></sup></span> Although the content of Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> in the SEI film on the PHC electrode is higher than that of FHCT<sub>2</sub>, Cheng et al. demonstrated by first-principles calculations that the diffusion barrier of Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> for sodium-ion transport is higher than that of NaF.<span><sup><a href="#cey2503-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2503-bib-0049_R_d76722569e1728" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - Chem Eng J">49</a></sup></span> It is suggested that the SEI film on the F-doped electrode has a higher sodium-ion conductivity than that on the PHC counterpart, which is responsible for its distinctly enhanced rate performances. In addition, the higher inorganic composition content allows for a more uniform and stable SEI film on FHCT<sub>2</sub> electrode which, therefore, exhibits excellent cycling stability.</p>
            
            <p>The different SEI film composition caused by the F content of the electrodes inevitably leads to differences in its microstructure. First, we performed atomic force microscopy (AFM) tests on the surfaces of the two electrodes in the undischarged state respectively. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16</a>, the similar surface morphology ensures the consistency of the initial state. Therefore, the mechanical properties of SEI film on both the PHC and FHCT<sub>2</sub> electrodes in diglyme-based electrolytes after 100 cycles were measured by AFM, and the influence of F-doping on the structure of SEI film was further analyzed.<span><sup><a href="#cey2503-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2503-bib-0050_R_d76722569e1743" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Proc Natl Acad Sci USA">50</a></sup></span> Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2503-fig-0007">7A,D</a> shows an obviously more uniform and smoother particle morphology of the F-containing electrode after cycling than that of the F-free counterpart. The average roughness of the SEI films on the PHC and FHCT<sub>2</sub> electrodes can be calculated to be 51.8 and 29.1 nm (Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a>), respectively. Moreover, the elastic modulus of cycled electrodes is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2503-fig-0007">7B,E</a>. The elastic modulus of the SEI film formed on the FHCT<sub>2</sub> electrode is much higher than that on PHC, as intuitively reflected in the mappings. Seven sites were also chosen in each mapping to demonstrate the mechanical properties, and the corresponding force-displacement curves are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2503-fig-0007">7C,F</a>. It can be directly observed from the figure that the elastic modulus of SEI film on the FHCT<sub>2</sub> electrode is notably higher than that of PHC. In other words, the force-displacement curves of the FHCT<sub>2</sub> electrode-derived SEI film during loading and unloading exhibited elastic deformation with small displacements. However, under similar force loading, the force-displacement curves were not fully reversible for the SEI film formed on the PHC electrode. To quantify the mechanical properties, the average Young's modulus of the SEI film formed within the FHCT<sub>2</sub> system is ~1.79 times higher than that formed in another electrode, 6359 versus 3543 MPa (Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a>). Based on the significant change in Young's modulus values, it concludes that the FHCT<sub>2</sub> electrode will form a compact and robust SEI film. Such robust SEI film is propitious to inhibiting interfacial fracture and thus stabilizes sodium-ion storage. In contrast, the lower Young's modulus values of the PHC electrode suggest the formation of a loose and unstable SEI film, which will lead to the unstable performance of the electrode during the sodiation/desodiation process. It has been demonstrated that Young's modulus of inorganic materials is larger than that of most organic polymers.<span><sup><a href="#cey2503-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2503-bib-0051_R_d76722569e1775" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Energy Storage Mater">51</a></sup></span> Therefore, the higher Young's modulus of the FHCT<sub>2</sub> electrode-derived SEI film strongly suggests that the interfacial compositions have a higher inorganic content, corresponding to the reduction products of Na–F and Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, as shown by the depth-profiling XPS results.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="cey2503-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/3f5fca1f-ed00-44b1-ba60-709adcec211c/cey2503-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/3f5fca1f-ed00-44b1-ba60-709adcec211c/cey2503-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/3f24c44d-de80-4472-8908-6c1b1238ee8d/cey2503-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/3f5fca1f-ed00-44b1-ba60-709adcec211c/cey2503-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=cey2503-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fcey2.503" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">AFM analysis of SEI formed in two-electrode&nbsp;system. 3D morphology of AFM images of (A) PHC-based and (D) FHCT<sub>2</sub>-based systems. (B, E) The corresponding 2D maps of the elastic modulus. (C, F) The corresponding representative force-displacement curves for selected localization points of the SEI film formed on cycled electrodes. In situ EIS test after SEI stabilization and in-situ EIS curves of (G) PHC and (H) FHCT<sub>2</sub> electrode systems and the corresponding evolution of different types of resistance with SOC&nbsp;obtained from their fitting results.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            
            <p>The formation of SEI film can also cause changes in the electrode resistance, so we conducted in situ EIS after three cycles. All EIS curves are fitted by equivalent circuits (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>) and show the evolution of the different types of resistance with state of charge (SOC) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2503-fig-0007">7G,H</a>). For each type of resistance contribution, the <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> values are similar for different electrodes, which attests that <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> is mainly related to the resistance of the electrolyte.<span><sup><a href="#cey2503-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2503-bib-0052_R_d76722569e1826" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - ACS Appl Mater Interfaces">52</a></sup></span> The RSEI values of both PHC and FHCT<sub>2</sub> remain almost steady, which means that the formed SEI film is relatively stable in the initial stage. In this case, <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> only represents the charge transfer resistance of sodium-ion reduction. As shown in the figures, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> values of the electrodes tend to reduce with increasing depth of discharge and rise with increasing depth of charge. This phenomenon is probably attributed to the fact that the sodiation process increases the electric conductivity of the electrode material, which favors the electrochemical reaction kinetics. It is worth noting that compared to PHC, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of FHCT<sub>2</sub> is much smaller. As is well known, <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> is largely dependent on the properties of the electrode surface, such as the surface morphology and the structure of the electrical double layer or the composition in SEI film.<span><sup><a href="#cey2503-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2503-bib-0053_R_d76722569e1846" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - Langmuir">53</a></sup></span> The decrease in <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> may be related to the low content of insulating organic species (RCH<sub>2</sub>ONa) in the SEI film.<span><sup><a href="#cey2503-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2503-bib-0054_R_d76722569e1855" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - Nano Energy">54</a></sup></span> The impedance changes of the different electrodes after the first and fourth cycles were also compared. A slight increase in <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> can be found, which is mainly related to the continuous formation of SEI film during the cycling process. In contrast, this increase of FHCT<sub>2</sub> is much lighter, indicating that F-doping can effectively improve the stability of the SEI film. Moreover, <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> also decreases after cycling, which corresponds to the activation process of the electrodes.</p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="cey2503-sec-0080">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="cey2503-sec-0080-title">3 CONCLUSION</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, a series of FHCT<sub><i>X</i></sub> with adjustable F content and graphitization degree is synthesized by simple heat treatment. The effects of F-doping on the physicochemical properties of hard carbon materials are systematically analyzed, and it is demonstrated that F-doping leads to the increased concentration of defects and expands the layer spacing of graphitic microcrystallite, which contributes to providing more reversible capacity and facilitates the reaction kinetics, therefore benefiting fast sodium-ion storage and cycling stability. Meanwhile, it was verified that excessive F-doping will aggravate the enlargement of C–F bond length after sodiation, leading to structural distortion and accelerating capacity decay. To grasp a full-scale understanding of the outstanding performance of the FHCT<sub>2</sub> electrode, various electrochemical and in situ analysis techniques were used to explore the sodium storage mechanism. Remarkably, based on the results obtained using depth-profiling XPS, AFM, and in situ EIS measurements, we also confirmed that the electronic structure changes resulting from F-doping can induce the formation of a homogeneous, low-organic, and NaF-rich SEI film, which can effectively optimize the overall sodium storage performance of the hard carbon anode. Thus, the results not only provide a feasible optimization strategy for hard carbon anodes but also reframe the doping optimization strategy, providing new insights into studying the role of heteroatoms in energy storage.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
